  7897	
  7898	APICIUS
  7899	
  7900	Book VI
  7901	
  7902	
  7903	
  7904	
  7905	{Illustration: THE GREAT CRATER
  7906	
  7907	Found at Hildesheim in 1868. This and a number of other pieces form
  7908	the collection known as The Hildesheim Treasure, now at the Kaiser
  7909	Friedrich Museum, Berlin.
  7910	
  7911	This wine crater is entirely of silver, a piece of supreme workmanship
  7912	of Roman origin. Very delicate decoration, anticipating the
  7913	Renaissance: Winged griffins and other monsters, half ox, half lion,
  7914	at the base; aquatic animals, genii angling and spearing fish.
  7915	
  7916	There is a second vessel inside, acting as a liner, to take the weight
  7917	of the fluid off the decorated bowl. The complete weight is 9451.8
  7918	gr., but the inner liner is stamped CVM BASI PONDO XXXXI--41 pounds
  7919	with the base. The weight of silver pieces was inscribed as a check on
  7920	the slaves.
  7921	
  7922	The bowl is 0.36 meter (about 14-1/4 inches) in height and 0.353 meter
  7923	in diameter. It stands on the tripod which is depicted separately.}
  7924	
  7925	
  7926	
  7927	
  7928	{Illustration: THE DIONYSOS CUP
  7929	
  7930	The Dionysos head in the center and the two satyrs are modeled
  7931	realistically by a most able artist. Lion and lioness heads on the
  7932	other side. Hildesheim Treasure.}
  7933	
  7934	
  7935	
  7936	
  7937	BOOK VI. FOWL
  7938	
  7939	_Lib. VI. Aëropetes_ [1]
  7940	
  7941	
  7942	    CHAP.    I. OSTRICH.
  7943	    CHAP.   II. CRANE OR DUCK, PARTRIDGE, DOVES, WOOD PIGEON, SQUAB
  7944	                AND DIVERS BIRDS.
  7945	    CHAP.  III. THRUSH [2].
  7946	    CHAP.   IV. FIGPECKER [2].
  7947	    CHAP.    V. PEACOCK [2].
  7948	    CHAP.   VI. PHEASANT [2].
  7949	    CHAP.  VII. GOOSE.
  7950	    CHAP. VIII. CHICKEN.
  7951	
  7952	    [1] Tac., Tor. _Trophetes_; probably an error in their
  7953	    rendering. List. _Aëroptes_, Greek for Fowl.
  7954	
  7955	    [2] The titles of these chapters and the classification
  7956	    is not adhered in the text of Book VI. The chapters are
  7957	    actually inscribed as follows:
  7958	
  7959	    Chap. I, Ostrich; II, Crane or Duck, Partridge, Turtle
  7960	    Dove, Wood Pigeon, Squab and divers birds; III,
  7961	    Partridge, Heathcock (Woodcock), Turtle Dove; IV, Wood
  7962	    Pigeon, Squab [Domestic Fattened Fowl, Flamingo]; V,
  7963	    Sauce for divers birds; VI, Flamingo; VII, In Order That
  7964	    Birds May Not Be Spoiled; VIII, Goose; IX, Chicken.
  7965	
  7966	
  7967	
  7968	I
  7969	
  7970	OSTRICH
  7971	  _IN STRUTHIONE_
  7972	
  7973	
  7974	[210] BOILED OSTRICH
  7975	    _IN STRUTHIONE ELIXO_
  7976	
  7977	[A stock in which to cook ostrich] PEPPER, MINT, CUMIN, LEEKS [1],
  7978	CELERY SEED, DATES, HONEY, VINEGAR, RAISIN WINE, BROTH, A LITTLE OIL.
  7979	BOIL THIS IN THE STOCK KETTLE [with the ostrich, remove the bird when
  7980	done, strain the liquid] THICKEN WITH ROUX. [To this sauce] ADD THE
  7981	OSTRICH MEAT CUT IN CONVENIENT PIECES, SPRINKLE WITH PEPPER. IF YOU
  7982	WISH IT MORE SEASONED OR TASTY, ADD GARLIC [during coction].
  7983	
  7984	    [1] G.-V. _Cuminum_; Tor. _C., porrum_, which is more
  7985	    likely.
  7986	
  7987	
  7988	[211] ANOTHER OSTRICH STEW
  7989	    _ALITER [in] STRUTHIONE ELIXO_
  7990	
  7991	PEPPER, LOVAGE, THYME, ALSO SATURY, HONEY, MUSTARD, VINEGAR, BROTH AND
  7992	OIL.
  7993	
  7994	
  7995	
  7996	II
  7997	
  7998	CRANE, DUCK, PARTRIDGE, DOVE, WOOD PIGEON, SQUAB, AND DIVERS BIRDS
  7999	  _IN GRUE VEL ANATE PERDICE TURTURE PALUMBO COLUMBO ET DIVERSIS AVIBUS_
  8000	
  8001	
  8002	[212] CRANE OR DUCK
  8003	    _GRUEM VEL ANATEM_
  8004	
  8005	WASH [the fowl] AND DRESS IT NICELY [1] PUT IN A STEW POT, ADD WATER,
  8006	SALT AND DILL, PARBOIL [2] SO AS TO HAVE THEM HALF DONE, UNTIL THE
  8007	MEAT IS HARD, REMOVE THEM, PUT THEM IN A SAUCE PAN [to be finished by
  8008	braising] WITH OIL, BROTH, A BUNCH OF ORIGANY AND CORIANDER; WHEN
  8009	NEARLY DONE, ADD A LITTLE REDUCED MUST, TO GIVE IT COLOR. MEANWHILE
  8010	CRUSH PEPPER, LOVAGE, CUMIN, CORIANDER, LASER ROOT, RUE [moistened
  8011	with] REDUCED WINE AND SOME HONEY, ADD SOME OF THE FOWL BROTH [3] TO
  8012	IT AND VINEGAR TO TASTE; EMPTY [the sauce] INTO A SAUCE PAN, HEAT,
  8013	BIND WITH ROUX, AND [strain] THE SAUCE OVER THE FOWL IN AN ENTRÉE
  8014	DISH.
  8015	
  8016	    [1] _Lavas et ornas_, i.e., singe, empty carcass of
  8017	    intestines, truss or bind it to keep its shape during
  8018	    coction, and, usually, lard it with either strips or
  8019	    slices of fat pork and stuff the carcass with greens,
  8020	    celery leaves, etc.
  8021	
  8022	    [2] _Dimidia coctura decoques._ Apicius here pursues the
  8023	    right course for the removable of any disagreeable taste
  8024	    often adhering to aquatic fowl, feeding on fish or food
  8025	    found in the water, by parboiling the meat. Cf. ℞ No.
  8026	    214.
  8027	
  8028	    [3] Again, as so often: _ius de suo sibi_; here the
  8029	    liquor of the braising pan, for stock in which the fowl
  8030	    is parboiled cannot be used for reasons set forth in
  8031	    Note 2.
  8032	
  8033	
  8034	[213] ANOTHER WAY OF COOKING CRANE, DUCK OR CHICKEN
  8035	    _ALITER IN GRUE [VEL] IN ANATE VEL IN PULLO_
  8036	
  8037	PEPPER, SHALLOTS, LOVAGE, CUMIN, CELERY SEED, PRUNES OR DAMASCUS PLUMS
  8038	STONES REMOVED, FRESH MUST, VINEGAR [1] BROTH, REDUCED MUST AND OIL.
  8039	BOIL THE CRANE; WHILE COOKING IT TAKE CARE THAT ITS HEAD IS NOT
  8040	TOUCHED BY THE WATER BUT THAT IT REMAINS WITHOUT. WHEN THE CRANE IS
  8041	DONE, WRAP IT IN A HOT TOWEL, AND PULL THE HEAD OFF SO THAT THE SINEWS
  8042	FOLLOW IN A MANNER THAT THE MEAT AND THE BONES REMAIN; FOR ONE CANNOT
  8043	ENJOY THE HARD SINEWS [2].
  8044	
  8045	    [1] Dann. mead.
  8046	
  8047	    [2] Remarkable ingenuity! Try this on your turkey legs.
  8048	    Danneil is of the opinion that the head and its feathers
  8049	    were to be saved for decorative purposes, in style
  8050	    during the middle ages when game bird patties were
  8051	    decorated with the fowl's plumage, a custom which
  8052	    survived to Danneil's time (ca. 1900). But this is not
  8053	    likely to be the case here, for it would be a simple
  8054	    matter to skin the bird before cooking it in order to
  8055	    save the plumage for the taxidermist.
  8056	
  8057	
  8058	[214] CRANE OR DUCK WITH TURNIPS
  8059	    _GRUEM VEL ANATEM EX RAPIS_ [1]
  8060	
  8061	TAKE OUT [remove entrails, [2]] CLEAN WASH AND DRESS [the bird] AND
  8062	PARBOIL [2] IT IN WATER WITH SALT AND DILL. NEXT PREPARE TURNIPS AND
  8063	COOK THEM IN WATER WHICH IS TO BE SQUEEZED OUT [3]. TAKE THEM OUT OF
  8064	THE POT AND WASH THEM AGAIN [4]. AND PUT INTO A SAUCE PAN THE DUCK
  8065	WITH OIL, BROTH, A BUNCH OF LEEKS AND CORIANDER; THE TURNIPS CUT INTO
  8066	SMALL PIECES; THESE PUT ON TOP OF THE [duck] IN ORDER TO FINISH
  8067	COOKING. WHEN HALF DONE, TO GIVE IT COLOR, ADD REDUCED MUST. THE SAUCE
  8068	IS PREPARED SEPARATELY: PEPPER, CUMIN, CORIANDER, LASER ROOT MOISTENED
  8069	WITH VINEGAR AND DILUTED WITH ITS OWN BROTH [of the fowl]; BRING THIS
  8070	TO A BOILING POINT, THICKEN WITH ROUX. [In a deep dish arrange the
  8071	duck] ON TOP OF THE TURNIPS [strain the sauce over it] SPRINKLE WITH
  8072	PEPPER AND SERVE.
  8073	
  8074	    [1] Duck and Turnips, a dish much esteemed on the
  8075	    Continent today. Only few prepare it correctly as does
  8076	    Old Apicius; hence it is not popular with the multitude.
  8077	
  8078	    [2] Tac., Tor. _excipies_; Hum. _legendum: ex rapis_.
  8079	
  8080	    [3] G.-V. _ut exbromari possint_; Tor. _expromi_; Hum.
  8081	    _expromari_; all of which does not mean anything. To
  8082	    cook the turnips so that they can be squeezed out
  8083	    (_exprimo_, from _ex_ and _premo_) is the proper thing
  8084	    to do from a culinary standpoint.
  8085	
  8086	    [4] The turnips are cooked half, the water removed, and
  8087	    finished with the duck, as prescribed by Apicius. It is
  8088	    really admirable to see how he handles these food
  8089	    materials in order to remove any disagreeable flavor,
  8090	    which may be the case both with the turnips (the small
  8091	    white variety) and the duck. Such careful treatment is
  8092	    little known nowadays even in the best kitchens. Cf.
  8093	    Note 2 to ℞ No. 212.
  8094	
  8095	
  8096	[215] ANOTHER [SAUCE FOR] CRANE OR DUCK
  8097	    _ALITER IN GRUEM VEL ANATEM ELIXAM_
  8098	
  8099	PEPPER, LOVAGE, CUMIN, DRY CORIANDER, MINT, ORIGANY, PINE NUTS, DATES,
  8100	BROTH, OIL, HONEY, MUSTARD AND WINE [1].
  8101	
  8102	    [1] Supposedly the ingredients for a sauce in which the
  8103	    parboiled fowl is braised and served.
  8104	
  8105	
  8106	[216] ROAST CRANE OR DUCK
  8107	    _ALITER GRUEM VEL ANATEM ASSAM_
  8108	
  8109	POUR OVER [the roast bird] THIS GRAVY: CRUSH PEPPER, LOVAGE, ORIGANY
  8110	WITH BROTH, HONEY, A LITTLE VINEGAR AND OIL; BOIL IT WELL, THICKEN
  8111	WITH ROUX [strain] IN THIS SAUCE PLACE SMALL PIECES OF PARBOILED
  8112	PUMPKIN OR COLOCASIUM [1] SO THAT THEY ARE FINISHED IN THE SAUCE; ALSO
  8113	COOK WITH IT CHICKEN FEET AND GIBLETS (all of which) SERVE IN A
  8114	CHAFING DISH, SPRINKLE WITH FINE PEPPER AND SERVE.
  8115	
  8116	    [1] Cf. ℞ Nos. 74, 216, 244, 322.
  8117	
  8118	
  8119	[217] BOILED CRANE OR DUCK IN ANOTHER MANNER
  8120	    _ALITER IN GRUE VEL ANATE ELIXA_
  8121	
  8122	PEPPER, LOVAGE, CELERY SEED, ROCKET, OR CORIANDER, MINT, DATES, HONEY,
  8123	VINEGAR, BROTH, REDUCED MUST AND MUSTARD. LIKEWISE USED FOR FOWL ROAST
  8124	[braised] IN THE POT.
  8125	
  8126	
  8127	
  8128	III
  8129	
  8130	WAYS TO PREPARE PARTRIDGE, HEATH-COCK OR WOODCOCK, AND BOILED TURTLE-DOVE
  8131	  _IN PERDICE ET ATTAGENA ET IN TURTURE ELIXIS_
  8132	
  8133	
  8134	[218] PARTRIDGE
  8135	    _IN PERDICE_
  8136	
  8137	PEPPER, LOVAGE, CELERY SEED, MINT, MYRTLE BERRIES, ALSO RAISINS, HONEY
  8138	[1] WINE, VINEGAR, BROTH, AND OIL. USE IT COLD [2] THE PARTRIDGE IS
  8139	SCALDED WITH ITS FEATHERS, AND WHILE WET THE FEATHERS ARE TAKEN OFF;
  8140	[the hair singed] IT IS THEN COOKED IN ITS OWN JUICE [braised] AND
  8141	WHEN DONE WILL NOT BE HARD IF CARE IS TAKEN [to baste it]. SHOULD IT
  8142	REMAIN HARD [if it is old] YOU MUST CONTINUE TO COOK IT UNTIL IT IS
  8143	TENDER.
  8144	
  8145	    [1] Honey wanting in Tor.
  8146	
  8147	    [2] G.-V. _Aliter_. This is one formula.
  8148	
  8149	
  8150	[219] [SAUCE] FOR PARTRIDGE, HEATH-COCK AND TURTLE-DOVE
  8151	    _IN PERDICE ET ATTAGENA ET IN TURTURE_
  8152	
  8153	PEPPER, LOVAGE, MINT, RUE SEED, BROTH, PURE WINE, AND OIL, HEATED.
  8154	
  8155	
  8156	
  8157	IV
  8158	
  8159	WOOD PIGEONS, SQUABS, FATTENED FOWL, FLAMINGO
  8160	  _IN PALUMBIS COLUMBIS AVIBUS IN ALTILE ET IN FENICOPTERO_
  8161	
  8162	
  8163	[220] FOR ROASTS: PEPPER, LOVAGE, CORIANDER, CARRAWAY,
  8164	      SHALLOTS, MINT, YOLKS OF EGG, DATES, HONEY,
  8165	      VINEGAR, BROTH, OIL AND WINE.
  8166	
  8167	
  8168	[221] ANOTHER [sauce] FOR BOILED [birds]
  8169	    _ALITER IN ELIXIS_
  8170	
  8171	TO THE BOILED FOWL ADD [1] PEPPER, CARRAWAY, CELERY SEED, PARSLEY,
  8172	CONDIMENTS, MORTARIA [2] DATES, HONEY, VINEGAR, WINE, OIL AND MUSTARD.
  8173	
  8174	    [1] Tor. wanting in other texts.
  8175	
  8176	    [2] _Mortaria_: herbs, spices, things pounded in the
  8177	    "mortar." Cf. ℞ No. 38.
  8178	
  8179	
  8180	[222] ANOTHER [sauce]
  8181	    _ALITER_
  8182	
  8183	PEPPER, LOVAGE, PARSLEY, CELERY SEED, RUE, PINE NUTS, DATES, HONEY,
  8184	VINEGAR, BROTH, MUSTARD AND A LITTLE OIL.
  8185	
  8186	
  8187	[223] ANOTHER [sauce]
  8188	    _ALITER_
  8189	
  8190	PEPPER, LOVAGE, LASER, WINE [1] MOISTENED WITH BROTH. ADD WINE AND
  8191	BROTH TO TASTE. MASK THE WOOD PIGEON OR SQUAB WITH IT. SPRINKLE WITH
  8192	PEPPER [2] AND SERVE.
  8193	
  8194	    [1] Tac., Tor. _laserum, vinum_; G.-V. _l. vivum_.
  8195	
  8196	    [2] Wanting in Tor.
  8197	
  8198	
  8199	
  8200	V
  8201	
  8202	
  8203	[224] SAUCE FOR DIFFERENT BIRDS
  8204	    _IUS IN DIVERSIS AVIBUS_
  8205	
  8206	PEPPER, DRY CUMIN, CRUSHED. LOVAGE, MINT, SEEDLESS RAISINS OR DAMASCUS
  8207	PLUMS, LITTLE HONEY, MYRTLE WINE TO TASTE, VINEGAR, BROTH, AND OIL.
  8208	HEAT AND WHIP IT WELL WITH CELERY AND SATURY [1].
  8209	
  8210	    [1] For centuries sauce whips were made of dry and green
  8211	    twigs, the bark of which was carefully peeled off.
  8212	
  8213	
  8214	[225] ANOTHER SAUCE FOR FOWL
  8215	    _ALITER IUS IN AVIBUS_
  8216	
  8217	PEPPER, LOVAGE, PARSLEY, DRY MINT, FENNEL BLOSSOMS [1] MOISTENED WITH
  8218	WINE; ADD ROASTED NUTS FROM PONTUS [2] OR ALMONDS, A LITTLE HONEY,
  8219	WINE, VINEGAR, AND BROTH TO TASTE. PUT OIL IN A POT, AND HEAT AND STIR
  8220	THE SAUCE, ADDING GREEN CELERY SEED, CAT-MINT; CARVE THE FOWL AND
  8221	COVER WITH THE SAUCE [3].
  8222	
  8223	    [1] Dann. _Cnecus_.
  8224	
  8225	    [2] Turkish hazelnuts.
  8226	
  8227	    [3] Tor. continuing without interruption.
  8228	
  8229	
  8230	[226] WHITE SAUCE FOR BOILED FOWL
  8231	    _IUS CANDIDUM IN AVEM ELIXAM_
  8232	
  8233	PEPPER, LOVAGE, CUMIN, CELERY SEED, TOASTED NUTS FROM PONTUS, OR
  8234	ALMONDS, ALSO SHELLED PINE NUTS, HONEY [1] A LITTLE BROTH, VINEGAR AND
  8235	OIL.
  8236	
  8237	    [1] Tor. _vel_; List. _mel_.
  8238	
  8239	
  8240	[227] GREEN SAUCE FOR FOWL
  8241	    _IUS VIRIDE IN AVIBUS_
  8242	
  8243	PEPPER, CARRAWAY, INDIAN SPIKENARD, CUMIN, BAY LEAVES, ALL KINDS OF
  8244	GREEN HERBS, DATES, HONEY, VINEGAR, WINE, LITTLE BROTH, AND OIL.
  8245	
  8246	
  8247	[228] WHITE SAUCE FOR BOILED GOOSE
  8248	    _IUS CANDIDUM IN ANSERE ELIXO_
  8249	
  8250	PEPPER, CARRAWAY, CUMIN, CELERY SEED, THYME, ONION, LASER ROOT,
  8251	TOASTED NUTS, HONEY, VINEGAR, BROTH AND OIL [1]
  8252	
  8253	    [1] A "sweet-sour" white sauce with herbs and spices is
  8254	    often served with goose in northern Germany.
  8255	
  8256	
  8257	[229] TREATMENT OF STRONG SMELLING BIRDS OF EVERY DESCRIPTION
  8258	    _AD AVES HIRCOSAS _[1]_ OMNI GENERE_
  8259	
  8260	FOR BIRDS OF ALL KINDS THAT HAVE A GOATISH [1] SMELL [2] PEPPER,
  8261	LOVAGE, THYME, DRY MINT, SAGE, DATES, HONEY, VINEGAR, WINE, BROTH,
  8262	OIL, REDUCED MUST, MUSTARD. THE BIRDS WILL BE MORE LUSCIOUS AND
  8263	NUTRITIOUS, AND THE FAT PRESERVED, IF YOU ENVELOP THEM IN A DOUGH OF
  8264	FLOUR AND OIL AND BAKE THEM IN THE OVEN [3].
  8265	
  8266	    [1] Probably game birds in an advanced stage of "_haut
  8267	    goût_" (as the Germans use the antiquated French term),
  8268	    or "_mortification_" as the French cook says. Possibly
  8269	    also such birds as crows, black birds, buzzards, etc.,
  8270	    and fish-feeding fowl. Moreover, it must be borne in
  8271	    mind that the refrigeration facilities of the ancients
  8272	    were not too good and that fresh goods spoiled quickly.
  8273	    Hence, perhaps, excessive seasoning, at least, as
  8274	    compared to our modern methods.
  8275	
  8276	    List. _aves piscivoras_; Hum. thinks the birds to be
  8277	    downright spoiled: _olidas, rancidas, & grave olentes_.
  8278	
  8279	    [2] Tor. Sentence wanting in other texts.
  8280	
  8281	    [3] For birds with a goatish smell Apicius should have
  8282	    repeated his excellent formula in ℞ No. 212, the
  8283	    method of parboiling the birds before final coction, if,
  8284	    indeed, one cannot dispense with such birds altogether.
  8285	    The above recipe does not in the least indicate how to
  8286	    treat smelly birds. Wrapping them in dough would vastly
  8287	    increase the ill-savour.
  8288	
  8289	    As for game birds, we agree with most connoisseurs that
  8290	    they should have just a suspicion of "_haut goût_"--a
  8291	    condition of advanced mellowness after the _rigor
  8292	    mortis_ has disappeared.
  8293	
  8294	
  8295	[230] ANOTHER TREATMENT OF ODOR
  8296	    _ALIUD CONTRA UIROSUM ODOREM_ [1]
  8297	
  8298	[IF THE BIRDS SMELL, [1]] STUFF THE INSIDE WITH CRUSHED FRESH OLIVES,
  8299	SEW UP [the aperture] AND THUS COOK, THEN RETIRE THE COOKED OLIVES.
  8300	
  8301	    [1] Tor.; other texts _aliter avem_, i.e. that the olive
  8302	    treatment is not necessarily confined to ill smelling
  8303	    birds alone.
  8304	
  8305	
  8306	
  8307	VI
  8308	
  8309	
  8310	[231] FOR FLAMINGO [and Parrot]
  8311	    _IN PHŒNICOPTERO_
  8312	
  8313	SCALD [1] THE FLAMINGO, WASH AND DRESS IT, PUT IT IN A POT, ADD WATER,
  8314	SALT, DILL, AND A LITTLE VINEGAR, TO BE PARBOILED. FINISH COOKING WITH
  8315	A BUNCH OF LEEKS AND CORIANDER, AND ADD SOME REDUCED MUST TO GIVE IT
  8316	COLOR. IN THE MORTAR CRUSH PEPPER, CUMIN, CORIANDER, LASER ROOT, MINT,
  8317	RUE, MOISTEN WITH VINEGAR, ADD DATES, AND THE FOND OF THE BRAISED
  8318	BIRD, THICKEN, [strain] COVER THE BIRD WITH THE SAUCE AND SERVE.
  8319	PARROT IS PREPARED IN THE SAME MANNER.
  8320	
  8321	    [1] Prior to removing the feathers; also singe the fine
  8322	    feathers and hair.
  8323	
  8324	
  8325	[232] ANOTHER WAY
  8326	    _ALITER_
  8327	
  8328	ROAST THE BIRD. CRUSH PEPPER, LOVAGE, CELERY SEED, SESAM [1] PARSLEY,
  8329	MINT, SHALLOTS, DATES, HONEY, WINE, BROTH, VINEGAR, OIL, REDUCED MUST
  8330	TO TASTE.
  8331	
  8332	    [1] Tor. _sesamum, defrutum_; G.-V. _s. frictum_.
  8333	
  8334	
  8335	
  8336	VII
  8337	
  8338	
  8339	[233] TO PREVENT BIRDS FROM SPOILING
  8340	    _AVES OMNES NE LIQUESCANT_
  8341	
  8342	SCALDED WITH THE FEATHERS BIRDS WILL NOT ALWAYS BE JUICY; IT IS BETTER
  8343	TO FIRST EMPTY THEM THROUGH THE NECK AND STEAM THEM SUSPENDED OVER A
  8344	KETTLE WITH WATER [1].
  8345	
  8346	    [1] Dry picking is of course the best method. Apicius is
  8347	    trying to overcome the evils of scalding fowl with the
  8348	    feathers. This formula is mutilated; the various texts
  8349	    differ considerably.
  8350	
  8351	
  8352	
  8353	VIII
  8354	
  8355	[FOR GOOSE]
  8356	  [_IN ANSERE_]
  8357	
  8358	
  8359	[234] BOILED GOOSE WITH COLD APICIAN SAUCE
  8360	    _ANSEREM ELIXUM EX IURE APICIANO FRIGIDO_
  8361	
  8362	CRUSH PEPPER, LOVAGE, CORIANDER SEED [1] MINT, RUE, MOISTEN WITH BROTH
  8363	AND A MODERATE AMOUNT OF OIL. TAKE THE COOKED GOOSE OUT OF THE POT AND
  8364	WHILE HOT WIPE IT CLEAN WITH A TOWEL, POUR THE SAUCE OVER IT AND
  8365	SERVE.
  8366	
  8367	    [1] G.-V.; Tor. (fresh) coriander, more suited for a
  8368	    cold sauce.
  8369	
  8370	
  8371	
  8372	IX
  8373	
  8374	[FOR CHICKEN]
  8375	  [_IN PULLO_]
  8376	
  8377	
  8378	[235] RAW SAUCE FOR BOILED CHICKEN
  8379	    _IN PULLO ELIXO IUS CRUDUM_
  8380	
  8381	PUT IN THE MORTAR DILL SEED, DRY MINT, LASER ROOT, MOISTEN WITH
  8382	VINEGAR, FIG WINE, BROTH, A LITTLE MUSTARD, OIL AND REDUCED MUST, AND
  8383	SERVE [1] [Known as] DILL CHICKEN [2].
  8384	
  8385	    [1] This and the preceding cold dressings are more or
  8386	    less variations of our modern cold dressings that are
  8387	    used for cold dishes of all kinds, especially salads.
  8388	
  8389	    [2] Tor. heads the following formula _præparatio pulli
  8390	    anethi_--chicken in dill sauce, which is the correct
  8391	    description of the above formula. Tac., G.-V. also
  8392	    commence the next with _pullum anethatum_, which is not
  8393	    correct, as the following recipe contains no dill.
  8394	
  8395	
  8396	[236] ANOTHER CHICKEN
  8397	    _ALITER PULLUS_ [1]
  8398	
  8399	A LITTLE HONEY IS MIXED WITH BROTH; THE COOKED [parboiled] CHICKEN IS
  8400	CLEANED [skin taken off, sinews, etc., removed] THE CARCASS DRIED WITH
  8401	A TOWEL, QUARTERED, THE PIECES IMMERSED IN BROTH [2] SO THAT THE
  8402	SAVOUR PENETRATES THOROUGHLY. FRY THE PIECES [in the pan] POUR OVER
  8403	THEIR OWN GRAVY, SPRINKLE WITH PEPPER, SERVE.
  8404	
  8405	    [1] Hum., List. cf. Note 2 to ℞ No. 235.
  8406	
  8407	    [2] Marinated; but the nature of this marinade is not
  8408	    quite clear; a spicy marinade of wine and herbs and
  8409	    spices would be appropriate for certain game birds, but
  8410	    chicken ordinarily requires no marinade except some oil
  8411	    before frying. It is possible that Apicius left the
  8412	    cooked chicken in the broth to prevent it from drying
  8413	    out, which is good.
  8414	
  8415	
  8416	[237] CHICKEN PARTHIAN STYLE
  8417	    _PULLUM PARTHICUM_ [1]
  8418	
  8419	DRESS THE CHICKEN CAREFULLY [2] AND QUARTER IT. CRUSH PEPPER, LOVAGE
  8420	AND A LITTLE CARRAWAY [3] MOISTENED WITH BROTH, AND ADD WINE TO TASTE.
  8421	[After frying] PLACE THE CHICKEN IN AN EARTHEN DISH [4] POUR THE
  8422	SEASONING OVER IT, ADD LASER AND WINE [5] LET IT ASSIMILATE WITH THE
  8423	SEASONING AND BRAISE THE CHICKEN TO A POINT. WHEN DONE SPRINKLE WITH
  8424	PEPPER AND SERVE.
  8425	
  8426	    [1] Lister is of the opinion that the _pullus Parthicus_
  8427	    is a kind of chicken that came originally from Asia,
  8428	    Parthia being a country of Asia, the present Persia or
  8429	    northern India, a chicken of small size with feathers on
  8430	    its feet, i.e., a bantam.
  8431	
  8432	    [2] Pluck, singe, empty, wash, trim. The texts: _a
  8433	    navi_. Hum. _hoc est, à parte posteriore ventris, qui ut
  8434	    navis cavus & figuræ ejus non dissimile est_. Dann.
  8435	    takes this literally, but _navo_ (_navus_) here simply
  8436	    means "to perform diligently."
  8437	
  8438	    [3] Tor. _casei modicum_; List. _carei_--more likely
  8439	    than cheese.
  8440	
  8441	    [4] _Cumana_--an earthenware casserole, excellent for
  8442	    that purpose.
  8443	
  8444	    [5] G.-V. _laser [et] vivum_.
  8445	
  8446	
  8447	[238] CHICKEN SOUR
  8448	    _PULLUM OXYZOMUM_
  8449	
  8450	A GOOD-SIZED GLASS OF OIL, A SMALLER GLASS OF BROTH, AND THE SMALLEST
  8451	MEASURE OF VINEGAR, 6 SCRUPLES OF PEPPER, PARSLEY AND A BUNCH OF
  8452	LEEKS.
  8453	
  8454	    G.-V. _[laseris] satis modice_.
  8455	
  8456	    These directions are very vague. If the raw chicken is
  8457	    quartered, fried in the oil, and then braised in the
  8458	    broth with a dash of vinegar, the bunch of leeks and
  8459	    parsley, seasoned with pepper and a little salt, we have
  8460	    a dish gastronomically correct. The leeks may be served
  8461	    as a garnish, the gravy, properly reduced and strained
  8462	    over the chicken which like in the previous formula is
  8463	    served in a casserole.
  8464	
  8465	
  8466	[239] GUINEA HEN
  8467	    _PULLUM NUMIDICUM_
  8468	
  8469	PREPARE [1] THE CHICKEN [as usual; par-] BOIL IT; CLEAN IT [2]
  8470	SEASONED WITH LASER AND PEPPER, AND FRY [in the pan; next] CRUSH
  8471	PEPPER, CUMIN, CORIANDER SEED, LASER ROOT, RUE, FIG DATES AND NUTS,
  8472	MOISTENED WITH VINEGAR, HONEY, BROTH AND OIL TO TASTE [3] WHEN BOILING
  8473	THICKEN WITH ROUX [strain] POUR OVER THE CHICKEN, SPRINKLE WITH PEPPER
  8474	AND SERVE.
  8475	
  8476	    [1] _Curas._
  8477	
  8478	    [2] Remove skin, tissues, bones, etc., cut in pieces
  8479	    and marinate in the pickle.
  8480	
  8481	    [3] Immerse the chicken pieces in this sauce and braise
  8482	    them to a point.
  8483	
  8484	
  8485	[240] CHICKEN WITH LASER
  8486	    _PULLUM LASERATUM_
  8487	
  8488	DRESS THE CHICKEN CAREFULLY [1] CLEAN, GARNISH [2] AND PLACE IN AN
  8489	EARTHEN CASSEROLE. CRUSH PEPPER, LOVAGE, LASER MOISTENED WITH WINE [3]
  8490	ADD BROTH AND WINE TO TASTE, AND PUT THIS ON THE FIRE; WHEN DONE SERVE
  8491	WITH PEPPER SPRINKLED OVER.
  8492	
  8493	    [1] _a navi._ cf. Note 2 to ℞ No. 237.
  8494	
  8495	    [2] G.-V. _lavabis_, _ornabis_, with vegetables, etc.
  8496	
  8497	    [3] G.-V. _laser vivum_.
  8498	
  8499	
  8500	[241] ROAST CHICKEN
  8501	    _PULLUM PAROPTUM_
  8502	
  8503	A LITTLE LASER, 6 SCRUPLES OF PEPPER, A GLASS OF OIL, A GLASS OF
  8504	BROTH, AND A LITTLE PARSLEY.
  8505	
  8506	    [1] _Paropsis_, _parapsis_, from the Greek, a platter,
  8507	    dish.
  8508	
  8509	    A most incomplete formula. It does not state whether the
  8510	    ingredients are to be added to the sauce or the
  8511	    dressing. We have an idea that the chicken is pickled in
  8512	    this solution before roasting and that the pickle is
  8513	    used in making the gravy.
  8514	
  8515	
  8516	[242] BOILED CHICKEN IN ITS OWN BROTH
  8517	    _PULLUM ELIXUM EX IURE SUO_
  8518	
  8519	CRUSH PEPPER, CUMIN, A LITTLE THYME, FENNEL SEED, MINT, RUE, LASER
  8520	ROOT, MOISTENED WITH VINEGAR, ADD FIG DATES [1] WORK WELL AND MAKE IT
  8521	SAVORY WITH HONEY, VINEGAR, BROTH AND OIL TO TASTE: THE BOILED CHICKEN
  8522	PROPERLY CLEANED AND DRIED [with the towel] IS MASKED WITH THIS SAUCE
  8523	[2].
  8524	
  8525	    [1] Goll. cloves--_cariophyllus_; the originals have
  8526	    _caryotam_ and _careotam_.
  8527	
  8528	    [2] Apparently another cold sauce of the vinaigrette
  8529	    type similar to ℞ No. 235.
  8530	
  8531	
  8532	[243] CHICKEN AND PUMPKIN
  8533	    _PULLUM ELIXUM CUM CUCURBITIS ELIXIS_
  8534	
  8535	TO THE ABOVE DESCRIBED DRESSING ADD MUSTARD, POUR OVER [1] AND SERVE.
  8536	
  8537	    [1] G.-V. _Perfundes_; Tor. _piper fundes_.
  8538	
  8539	    The pumpkin, not mentioned here, is likewise served cold
  8540	    boiled, seasoned with the same dressing. It is perhaps
  8541	    used for stuffing the chicken and cooked simultaneously
  8542	    with the same.
  8543	
  8544	
  8545	[244] CHICKEN AND DASHEENS [1]
  8546	    _PULLUM ELIXUM CUM COLOCASIIS ELIXIS_
  8547	
  8548	THE ABOVE SAUCE IS ALSO USED FOR THIS DISH. STUFF THE CHICKEN WITH
  8549	[peeled] DASHEENS AND [stoned] GREEN OLIVES, THOUGH NOT TOO MUCH SO
  8550	THAT THE DRESSING MAY HAVE ROOM FOR EXPANSION, TO PREVENT BURSTING
  8551	WHILE THE CHICKEN IS BEING COOKED IN THE POT. HOLD IT DOWN WITH A
  8552	SMALL BASKET, LIFT IT UP FREQUENTLY [2] AND HANDLE CAREFULLY SO THAT
  8553	THE CHICKEN DOES NOT BURST [3].
  8554	
  8555	    [1] Dasheens are the equivalent of the ancient
  8556	    colocasium; at least they are very close relatives. Cf.
  8557	    Notes to ℞ Nos. 74, 216, 244, 322.
  8558	
  8559	    [2] For inspection. G.-V. _levas_; Tor. _lavabis_, for
  8560	    which there is no reason.
  8561	
  8562	    [3] Dann. and Goll., not knowing the colocasium or
  8563	    dasheen have entirely erroneous versions of this
  8564	    formula. The dasheen is well adapted for the stuffing of
  8565	    fowl. Ordinarily the dasheen is boiled or steamed,
  8566	    mashed, seasoned and then stuffed inside of a raw
  8567	    chicken which is then roasted. Being very starchy, the
  8568	    dasheen readily absorbs the fats and juices of the
  8569	    roast, making a delicious dressing, akin in taste to a
  8570	    combined potato and chestnut purée.
  8571	
  8572	    As the above chicken is cooked in _bouillon_ or water,
  8573	    the dasheen may be used in a raw state for filling. We
  8574	    have tried this method. Instead of confining the chicken
  8575	    in a basket, we have tied it in a napkin and boiled
  8576	    slowly until done. Serve cold, with the above dressing.
  8577	
  8578	
  8579	[245] CHICKEN À LA VARUS [1]
  8580	    _PULLUS VARDANUS_
  8581	
  8582	COOK THE CHICKEN IN THIS STOCK: BROTH, OIL, WINE, A BUNCH OF LEEKS,
  8583	CORIANDER, SATURY; WHEN DONE, CRUSH PEPPER, NUTS WITH 2 GLASSES OF
  8584	WATER [2] AND THE JUICE OF THE CHICKEN. RETIRE THE BUNCHES OF GREENS,
  8585	ADD MILK TO TASTE. THE THINGS CRUSHED IN THE MORTAR ADD TO THE CHICKEN
  8586	AND COOK IT TOGETHER: THICKEN THE SAUCE WITH BEATEN WHITES OF EGG [3]
  8587	AND POUR THE SAUCE OVER THE CHICKEN. THIS IS CALLED "WHITE SAUCE."
  8588	
  8589	    [1] G.-V. _Vardanus_; Tor. _Vardamus_; Hum. _Vardanus
  8590	    legendum, puto, Varianus, portentuosæ luxuriæ
  8591	    Imperator_. Hum. thinks the dish is dedicated to emperor
  8592	    Varianus (?) The word may also be the adjective of
  8593	    Varus, Quintilius V., commander of colonial armies and
  8594	    glutton, under Augustus. Varus committed suicide after
  8595	    his defeat in the Teutoburg Forest by the Germans.
  8596	
  8597	    [2] G.-V. broth, own stock--_ius de suo sibi_.
  8598	
  8599	    [3] Strain, avoid ebullition after the eggs have been
  8600	    added. Most unusual _liaison_; usually the yolks are
  8601	    used for this purpose. The whites are consistent with
  8602	    the name of the sauce.
  8603	
  8604	
  8605	[246] CHICKEN À LA FRONTO [1]
  8606	    _PULLUM FRONTONIANUM_
  8607	
  8608	A HALF-COOKED CHICKEN MARINADED IN A PICKLE OF BROTH, MIXED WITH OIL,
  8609	TO WHICH IS ADDED A BUNCH OF DILL, LEEKS, SATURY AND GREEN CORIANDER.
  8610	FINISH IT IN THIS BROTH. WHEN DONE, TAKE THE CHICKEN OUT [2] DRESS IT
  8611	NICELY ON A DISH, POUR OVER THE [sauce, colored with] REDUCED MUST,
  8612	SPRINKLE WITH PEPPER AND SERVE.
  8613	
  8614	    [1] Named for a Roman by the name of Fronto. There is a
  8615	    sucking pig à la Fronto, too. Cf. ℞ No. 374. M.
  8616	    Cornelius Fronto was orator and author during the reign
  8617	    of Emperor Hadrian. According to Dann. a certain
  8618	    Frontone under Emperor Severus.
  8619	
  8620	    [2] List., G.-V. _levabis_; Tor. _lavabis_, for which
  8621	    there is little or no occasion. He may mean to clean,
  8622	    i.e. remove skin, tissues, sinews, small bones, etc.
  8623	
  8624	
  8625	[247] CREAMED CHICKEN WITH PASTE [1]
  8626	    _PULLUS TRACTOGALATUS_ [2]
  8627	
  8628	COOK THE CHICKEN [as follows, in] BROTH, OIL, WITH WINE ADDED, TO
  8629	WHICH ADD A BUNCH OF CORIANDER AND [green] ONIONS. WHEN DONE TAKE IT
  8630	OUT [3] [strain and save] THE BROTH, AND PUT IT IN A NEW SAUCE PAN,
  8631	ADD MILK AND A LITTLE SALT, HONEY AND A PINT [4] OF WATER, THAT IS, A
  8632	THIRD PART: PLACE IT BACK ON A SLOW FIRE TO SIMMER. FINALLY BREAK [the
  8633	paste, [1]] PUT IT LITTLE BY LITTLE INTO [the boiling broth] STIRRING
  8634	WELL SO IT WILL NOT BURN. PUT THE CHICKEN IN, EITHER WHOLE OR IN
  8635	PIECES [5] DISH IT OUT IN A DEEP DISH. THIS COVER WITH THE FOLLOWING
  8636	SAUCE [6] PEPPER, LOVAGE, ORIGANY, MOISTENED WITH HONEY AND A LITTLE
  8637	REDUCED MUST. ADD SOME OF THE [chicken] BROTH, HEAT IN A SMALL SAUCE
  8638	PAN AND WHEN IT BOILS THICKEN WITH ROUX [7] AND SERVE.
  8639	
  8640	    [1] Spätzle, noodles, macaroni; this dish is the ancient
  8641	    "Chicken Tetrazzini." Dann. Chicken pie or patty.
  8642	
  8643	    [2] _tractum_ and _gala_, prepared with paste and milk.
  8644	    Cf. _tractomelitus_, from _tractum_ and _meli_, paste
  8645	    and honey.
  8646	
  8647	    [3] Cf. Note 2 to ℞ Nos. 244 and 246.
  8648	
  8649	    [4] List. _minimum_; Tor. _heminam_; Sch. _eminam_. See
  8650	    Measures. The noodle paste should be cooked separately
  8651	    in the water.
  8652	
  8653	    [5] List. _vel carptum_, which is correct. Tor. _vel
  8654	    careotam_, out of place here.
  8655	
  8656	    [6] This sauce seems to be superfluous. Very likely it
  8657	    is a separate formula for a sauce of some kind.
  8658	
  8659	    [7] Seems superfluous, too. The noodle paste in the
  8660	    chicken gravy makes it sufficiently thick.
  8661	
  8662	
  8663	[248] STUFFED CHICKEN [OR PIG]
  8664	    _PULLUS FARSILIS_ [1]
  8665	
  8666	EMPTY THE CHICKEN THROUGH THE APERTURE OF THE NECK SO THAT NONE OF THE
  8667	ENTRAILS REMAIN. CRUSH PEPPER, LOVAGE, GINGER, CUT MEAT [2] COOKED
  8668	SPELT, BESIDES CRUSH BRAINS COOKED IN THE [chicken] BROTH, BREAK EGGS
  8669	AND MIX ALL TOGETHER IN ORDER TO MAKE A SOLID DRESSING; ADD BROTH TO
  8670	TASTE AND A LITTLE OIL, WHOLE PEPPER, PLENTY OF NUTS. WITH THIS
  8671	DRESSING STUFF EITHER A CHICKEN OR A SUCKLING PIG, LEAVING ENOUGH ROOM
  8672	FOR EXPANSION [3].
  8673	
  8674	    [1] Tor. _fusilis_.
  8675	
  8676	    [2] Preferably raw pork or veal.
  8677	
  8678	    [3] A most sumptuous dressing; it compares favorably
  8679	    with our popular stale bread pap usually called "chicken
  8680	    dressing."
  8681	
  8682	
  8683	[249] STUFFED CAPON LIKEWISE
  8684	    _SIMILITER IN CAPO FACIES_ [1]
  8685	
  8686	THE CAPON IS STUFFED IN A SIMILAR WAY BUT IS COOKED WITH ALL THE BONES
  8687	REMOVED [2].
  8688	
  8689	    [1] Sch. _in capso_. May be interpreted thus: Cooked in
  8690	    an envelope of caul or linen, in which case it would
  8691	    correspond to our modern galantine of chicken.
  8692	
  8693	    [2] Tor. _ossibus eiectis_; Hum. _omnibus e._; i.e. all
  8694	    the entrails, etc., which is not correct. The bones must
  8695	    be removed from the capon in this case.
  8696	
  8697	
  8698	[250] CHICKEN AND CREAM SAUCE [1]
  8699	    _PULLUS LEUCOZOMUS_ [2]
  8700	
  8701	TAKE A CHICKEN AND PREPARE IT AS ABOVE. EMPTY IT THROUGH THE APERTURE
  8702	OF THE NECK SO THAT NONE OF THE ENTRAILS REMAIN. TAKE [a little] WATER
  8703	[3] AND PLENTY OF SPANISH OIL, STIR, COOK TOGETHER UNTIL ALL MOISTURE
  8704	IS EVAPORATED [4] WHEN THIS IS DONE TAKE THE CHICKEN OUT, SO THAT THE
  8705	GREATEST POSSIBLE AMOUNT OF OIL REMAINS BEHIND [5] SPRINKLE WITH
  8706	PEPPER AND SERVE [6].
  8707	
  8708	    [1] The ancient version of Chicken à la Maryland, Wiener
  8709	    Backhähndl, etc.
  8710	
  8711	    [2] Tor. _Leocozymus_; from the Greek _leucozomos_,
  8712	    prepared with white sauce. The formula for the cream
  8713	    sauce is lacking here. Cf. ℞ No. 245.
  8714	
  8715	    [3] The use of water to clarify the oil which is to
  8716	    serve as a deep frying fat is an ingenious idea, little
  8717	    practised today. It surely saves the fat or oil,
  8718	    prevents premature burning or blackening by frequent
  8719	    use, and gives a better tasting _friture_. The above
  8720	    recipe is a mere fragment, but even this reveals the
  8721	    extraordinary knowledge of culinary principles of
  8722	    Apicius who reveals himself to us as a master of
  8723	    well-understood principles of good cookery that are so
  8724	    often ignored today. Cf. Note 5 to ℞ No. 497.
  8725	
  8726	    [4] The recipe fails to state that the chicken must be
  8727	    breaded, or that the pieces of chicken be turned in
  8728	    flour, etc., and fried in the oil.
  8729	
  8730	    [5] Another vital rule of deep fat frying not stated, or
  8731	    rather stated in the language of the kitchen, namely
  8732	    that the chicken must be crisp, dry, that is, not
  8733	    saturated with oil, which of course every good fry cook
  8734	    knows.
  8735	
  8736	    [6] With the cream sauce, prepared separately, spread on
  8737	    the platter, with the fried chicken inside, or the sauce
  8738	    in a separate dish, we have here a very close
  8739	    resemblance to a very popular modern dish.
  8740	
  8741	    (Schuch and Danneil insert here Excerpta XXIX, XXX and
  8742	    XXXI.)
  8743	
  8744	
  8745	END OF BOOK VI
  8746	
  8747	[explicit] _TROPHETES APICII. LIBER SEXTUS_ [Tac.]
  8748	
  8749	
  8750	
  8751	
  8752	{Illustration: FRYING PAN, ROUND
  8753	
  8754	Provided with a lip to pour out fluids, a convenience which many
  8755	modern pans lack. The broad flat handle is of one piece with the pan
  8756	and has a hole for suspension. On some ancient pans these handles were
  8757	hinged so as to fold over the cavity of the pan, to save room in
  8758	storing it away, particularly in a soldier's knapsack. Ntl. Mus.,
  8759	Naples, 76571; Field M. 24024.}
  8760	
  8761	
  8762	
  8763	
  8764	{Illustration: FRONTISPICE, SECOND LISTER EDITION
  8765	
  8766	purporting to represent the interior of an ancient kitchen. J.
  8767	Gœree, the artist and engraver, has invented it. The general
  8768	tidiness differs from contemporary Dutch kitchens and the clothing of
  8769	the cooks reminds one of Henry VIII, who issued at Eltham in 1526 this
  8770	order: "... provide and sufficiently furnish the kitchens of such
  8771	scolyons as shall not goe naked or in garments of such vilenesse as
  8772	they doe ... nor lie in the nights and dayes in the kitchens ... by
  8773	the fire-side...."--MS. No. 642, Harleian Library.}
  8774

  8776

  8778	APICIUS
  8779	
  8780	Book VII
  8781	
  8782	
  8783	
  8784	
  8785	{Illustration: THE GREAT PALLAS ATHENE DISH
  8786	
  8787	One of the finest show platters in existence. Of Hellenic make. The
  8788	object in the right hand of Athene has created considerable conjecture
  8789	but has never been identified.
  8790	
  8791	Hildesheim Treasure.}
  8792	
  8793	
  8794	
  8795	
  8796	{Illustration: FRYING PAN, OVAL
  8797	
  8798	This oblong pan was no doubt primarily used in fish cookery. An oblong
  8799	piece of food material fitted snugly into the pan, thus saving fats
  8800	and other liquids in preparation. Around the slender handle was no
  8801	doubt one of non-heat-conducting material. The shape and the lip of
  8802	the pan indicate that it was not used for "sauter." Ntl. Mus., Naples,
  8803	76602; Field M. 24038.}

  8808	BOOK VII. SUMPTUOUS DISHES
  8809

  8814	                AND FEET.

  8830	    CHAP. XVII. EGGS.
  8831
